width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #aabdef; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;0.350–0.554 (low)</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #a0a0a0; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Data unavailable</div> </td></tr></tbody></table></div></div></div>
<p>This is a full <b>list of countries by the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a></b> as included in a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">United Nations Development Programme</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Report" title="Human Development Report">Human Development Report</a>. The latest report was released on 14 September 2018 and is based on data collected in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-UNDP2018_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNDP2018-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 2010 Human Development Report, a further <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_inequality-adjusted_HDI" title="List of countries by inequality-adjusted HDI">Inequality-adjusted Human Development Index</a> (IHDI) was introduced. It stated that while the HDI remains useful, "the IHDI is the actual level of human development (accounting for inequality)" and "the HDI can be viewed as an index of "potential" human development (or the maximum IHDI that could be achieved if there were no inequality)".<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> The index does not take into account several factors, such as the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_wealth_per_adult" title="List of countries by wealth per adult">net wealth per capita</a> or the relative <a href="/wiki/Quality_(business)" title="Quality (business)">quality of goods</a> in a country. This situation tends to lower the ranking for some of the most advanced countries, such as the <a href="/wiki/G7" class="mw-redirect" title="G7">G7</a> members and others.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Methodology">Methodology</span></h2>

width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #2B0000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;− 0.010</div> </td></tr></tbody></table></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> (HDI) is a composite statistic of <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Education" title="Education">education</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Median_income" title="Median income">income per capita</a> indicators. A country scores higher HDI when the life expectancy at birth is longer, the education period is longer, and the income per capita is higher. It is used to distinguish whether the country is a <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">developed</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing</a> or <a href="/wiki/Least_developed_country" class="mw-redirect" title="Least developed country">an underdeveloped country</a>. The index was developed in 1990 by Pakistani <a href="/wiki/Economics" title="Economics">economist</a> <a href="/wiki/Mahbub_ul_Haq" title="Mahbub ul Haq">Mahbub ul Haq</a><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> and Indian economist <a href="/wiki/Amartya_Sen" title="Amartya Sen">Amartya Sen</a>.
The UN report covers 187 <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_United_Nations" title="Member states of the United Nations">member states of the United Nations</a> (out of 193), along with <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a> and <a href="/wiki/State_of_Palestine" title="State of Palestine">Palestine</a>; 7 UN member states are not included because of lack of data. The average HDI of regions of the world and groups of countries are also included for comparison.
</p><p>Countries fall into four broad human development categories: Very High Human Development, High Human Development, Medium Human Development and Low Human Development.
</p><p>Because of the new methodology adopted since the 2010 Human Development Report, the new reported HDI figures appear lower than the HDI figures in previous reports.
</p><p>From 2007 to 2010, the first category was referred to as developed countries, and the last three are all grouped in developing countries. The original "high human development" category has been split into two as above in the report for 2007.
</p><p>Some older groupings (<i>high/medium/low income countries</i>) that were based on the <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> (GDP) in <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a> (PPP) per capita have been replaced by another index based on the <a href="/wiki/Gross_national_income" title="Gross national income">gross national income</a> (GNI) in purchasing power parity per capita.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Frequency_of_issuing_the_index">Frequency of issuing the index</span></h2>
<p>The index was first published in 1990 along with the Human Development Report. Since then, each year the index has been updated except for the years 2012 and 2017, where no Human Development Report was issued. The indices for 2012 and 2017 were still both published in the following Human Development Report.
</p><p>The latest index — covering 189 countries — was launched on 14 September 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-UNDP2018_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNDP2018-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Countries_missing_from_latest_report">Countries missing from latest report</span></h2>
<p><b>Note</b>: The 2009 publication uses an older version of the HDI formula and classification standard. The ranges are 0–0.499 for low HDI, 0.500–0.799 for medium HDI, 0.800–0.899 for high HDI and greater than 0.900 for very high HDI.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-10">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The UN does not calculate the HDI of Macau. The government of Macau calculates its own HDI.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-13"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-13">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The UN <a href="/wiki/China_and_the_United_Nations" title="China and the United Nations">does not recognize</a> the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of China">Republic of China</a> (<a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>) as a <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a>. The HDI report does not include Taiwan as part of the People's Republic of China when calculating China's figures (see<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>). Taiwan's government calculated its HDI to be 0.907, based on 2010 new methodology of UNDP.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
